Paris Bloodshed Case: Daladier to be Summoned for Questioning 45

Former Interior Minister Also on the List of Those to Be Summoned

Radical Party Member of Parliament Arrested and Imprisoned for Bribery

(Paris) Today, the former Paris Police Chief, Chiappe, told the committee investigating the Paris riots last month that the former Minister of the Interior, Frot, in the Daladier cabinet, had planned to gather former members of the Communist Party and Royalists to support him. Therefore, he warned Prime Minister Daladier about this matter and informed him that the extreme left wing party had requested a certain wealthy cabinet member to provide military equipment and funding. Chiappe also detailed the tense situation before his resignation on February 3, saying that the Communist Party wanted to put him to death, and the streetcar workers' strike seemed to have received funding from some source. He also said that the police were loyal to the Republic and were very reliable. If he had not resigned on February 6, he believed that the bloody tragedy in Paris that day would not have occurred. After receiving this testimony, the investigation committee decided to summon former Prime Minister Daladier and former Interior Minister Frot on March 9 for questioning. If necessary, they will be confronted with Chiappe. Frot has now issued an article denying Chiappe's words, saying that Chiappe's words are more like a detective novel and not like a testimony in court. (Reuters, 8th)

(Paris) Radical Socialist Party member of parliament, Bonoure, was arrested and imprisoned by the court for receiving 100,000 francs from the notorious swindler Stavisky. The Radical Socialist Party Executive Committee has now expelled Bonoure from the party and decided to carry out a party purge to expel corrupt elements from the party. (Havas, 8th)

Page 8

President Wang Cables Guangdong, Stating Central Government's Attitude Towards Puppets 46

It is Fundamentally Not Recognized That They Have a Political Stance, Which is Internationally Acknowledged

If the Cable Sent by Guangdong is a Foreign Ultimatum, it Will Hinder Unification

(Nanjing) Regarding the puppet's usurpation of the title and the publication of a circular telegram by Chen Jitang and others, President Wang cabled Chen and others on the 8th, saying, "To Commissioner Gan of Guangzhou, Brother Jiehou, and forwarded to Commander-in-Chief Chen, Brother Bonan, and Chairman Lin, Brother Yungai, greetings. Reading the newspaper, I learned that you have issued a circular telegram regarding Puyi's claim to the throne. Although I have not seen the full text, I can imagine your righteous indignation and am very grateful. However, there are three important points that I would like to bring to your attention: (1) For the past two years, we have consistently recognized that the Northeast is under military occupation, and all political organizations are passive and no different from puppets. In other words, these puppets do not have the autonomous consciousness and ability to separate from the Republic of China. If the state of military occupation ends, these puppets will immediately be removed. Our position is based on facts and is not only recognized domestically but also internationally. (2) We fundamentally do not recognize the puppet state, regardless of its form of government. In other words, wearing a tailcoat and calling oneself a regent or wearing a dragon robe and calling oneself an emperor is the same kind of ridiculous puppet show, and it only highlights its ugliness. (3) If your circular telegram is meant to encourage comrades and inspire the people, then there is no objection. However, if it is a foreign ultimatum, it will hinder unification. In short, with the country in such dire straits, we have no room for emotional arguments. However, I must solemnly inform you of the government's policies and attitudes in the international arena for the past two years. I hope you will understand. Wang Zhaoming, Qi. (Central News Agency, 8th)"

Joint Circular Telegram from the Southwest Executive Department and the Political Council 47

(Guangzhou) The Southwest Executive Department of the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang and the Southwest Political Affairs Committee of the National Government issued a joint circular telegram on the 6th, opposing Puyi's usurpation of the throne. The text reads: "To the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Party Headquarters of all provinces and cities, the governments of all provinces and cities, all pacification directors, all commanders-in-chief, all commanders, all division and brigade commanders, all organizations, all groups, all newspapers, and all the people, greetings. The rebel Puyi, with the help of foreign forces, has occupied the Northeast and usurped the false title, changing from a regent to an emperor. His arrogance and absurdity are deeply resented. Our four northeastern provinces have suffered from the poison of foreign troops for nearly three years. The puppet has been on stage for two years. Now, we have something to tell our friendly nations: The three northeastern provinces and Rehe are part of the territory of the Republic of China. Puyi's claim to the throne in the Northeast with foreign help is self-destructive. The citizens of the Republic of China will resolutely seek to suppress and restore it. It is hoped that friendly nations in the East and West can uphold their past recognition, maintain their policy of non-recognition, and further take joint action to sanction those who promote internal strife, so as to uphold the common political justice of mankind and maintain the established international treaties. The peace of the Far East depends on it. Furthermore, we have something to tell our citizens: The revival of the Chinese nation depends on the ability of our citizens to save themselves. The current situation is difficult and dangerous, unprecedented in the history of our nation. We are deeply concerned about the current situation and earnestly hope that we can encourage each other to maintain the integrity of our country's territory and sovereignty, so that the Chinese nation can continue to survive in the world. This special circular telegram is issued so that both inside and outside can be aware of it. Respectfully, the Southwest Executive Department of the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang and the Southwest Political Affairs Committee of the National Government, K. (Delayed Far East News Agency, 6th)"

Three Committees of the Legislative Yuan Held a Joint Meeting Yesterday 54

Review of the Silver Agreement

Decision to Add an Annex

(Nanjing) The Foreign Affairs, Finance, and Economic Affairs Committees of the Legislative Yuan held a joint meeting on the 8th to review the Silver Agreement. Chairman Ma Yinchu. As a result of the resolution, an annex was added to Article 4 of the agreement, namely, that our country's monetary standard has the freedom to reform at any time and is not bound by the treaty. The text of the annex was drafted by Committee Member Ma, and it was revised and passed by the whole body on the spot. It was decided to submit it to the Legislative Yuan for discussion on the 9th. (Special dispatch, 8th)

(Nanjing) Regarding the Silver Agreement, the joint meeting of the Legislative Yuan on the 8th, based on the preliminary review conclusions and the opinions expressed by Ma Yinchu, passed the Silver Agreement for approval by our government. However, an additional condition was added after the original agreement: During the effective period of the agreement, if the price of silver rises sharply and has an adverse impact on China's finance and industry, the Chinese government may freely take appropriate action to protect its industry and reform its currency system. According to Ma Yinchu, although the addition of free conditions to the approval of the Silver Agreement reduces restrictions, the impact on our country after the price of silver rises is still great. Therefore, I advocate that the government quickly issue an order to prohibit the export of silver to deal with the situation. (Special dispatch, 8th)

Three Measures Agreed Upon for Handling Labor-Management Dispute Penalties 60

(Nanjing) The Shanghai Municipal Government submitted a case requesting the determination of the penalty-imposing agencies for the Trade Union Law, the Factory Law, and the Labor Dispute Handling Law to consolidate and maintain industry, and requesting that the fines be used for workers' welfare undertakings. After receiving the submission, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce consulted with the Ministry of Judicial Administration on the 8th and agreed on three measures: 1. The court should be the penalty-imposing agency; 2. 40% of the fines should be allocated for workers' welfare undertakings and a fixed standard should be established; 3. After receiving the court's notification, the trade union should submit the use of the funds to the competent authorities for approval and attach the approval documents to the court for collection. In addition to submitting the above points to the Executive Yuan for record, the Ministry of Judicial Administration will also instruct the higher courts of all provinces to comply. At the same time, it will also advise the governments of all provinces to comply on the same day. (Special dispatch, 8th)

Mongolian and Tibetan Council Cables Tibet to Inquire About the Truth of the Kang Incident 62

(Nanjing) It is widely rumored that Tibetan troops have launched a large-scale invasion of Kang, and Dengke County has been surrounded by Tibetan troops for several days. After the Central Government approved Liu Wenhui's telegram, it telegraphed Liu Xiang for assistance. According to Shi Qingyang, Chairman of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, when the Sichuan army recaptured Ganzi and Dajin in western Sichuan, all the lamas in the temples were driven away and wandered in western Sichuan, like bandits. Now that the national defense in western Sichuan is weak, they have an opportunity to take advantage of, so they have joined forces to invade in order to seize the temple and live in it. It has not yet been verified whether official Tibetan troops participated. Since receiving the telegram from Liu Wenhui, the committee has not only telegraphed Liu to strictly guard against it, but also telegraphed Liu Xiang, commander-in-chief of bandit suppression in Sichuan, to pay attention to the Kang army and coordinate countermeasures. At the same time, it has also telegraphed Reting Hutuktu, the head of the Tibetan government in Lhasa, to inquire about the truth in order to verify the facts. However, transportation is inconvenient in that area. It takes 40 days to transmit news back and forth from Lhasa to the Jinsha River. Therefore, the reply telegram will arrive in Beijing only after 40 days. (Special dispatch, 8th)

Ma Lin and Others Send Two Telegrams to the Central Government Requesting Bail for Jin Shuren 63

(Nanjing) Ma Lin, Ma Hongbin, Ma Bufang, and others telegraphed the Central Government again, saying that Jin Shuren was ill in custody and requested grace to be released for medical treatment, and requested leniency for Jin's crimes, saying that during the Yan Xishan Incident in the 17th year of the Republic of China, Jin quickly quelled the rebellion, alleviating the Central Government's concerns in the west. This one achievement is enough to pardon him ten times over. (Special dispatch, 8th)

The Revised Schedule for the Beijing-Shanghai Through Train 64

(Nanjing) The revised train schedule for the Beijing-Shanghai through train is scheduled to take effect on April 1. After that, the ferries between Nanjing and Pukou will operate at night. Train No. 301 will depart from Beijing at 3:05 PM every day and arrive in Shanghai in 40 and a half hours. Train No. 302 will depart from Shanghai at 4:00 PM and arrive in Beijing in 42 and a half hours. (Central News Agency, 8th)

Minutes of the Regular Meeting of the Examination Yuan 65

(Nanjing) The Examination Yuan held its 111th meeting on the 8th. Chairman Wang Yongbin resolved: (1) Approved the Zhejiang Department of Education to hold a general examination for educational administrative personnel and submitted it to the Executive Yuan for approval. (2) Passed the application qualifications for the higher examination, with 9 people passing the review, and 67 people for the general talent examination. (Central News Agency, 8th)

Meteorological Observatories Will Be Established in Taishan, Chuan, and Suzhou 66

(Nanjing) The Central Meteorological Research Institute plans to establish an observatory in Taishan. Last month, it sent Zhuge Zhenggong and Liu Futai, the head of the Department of Architecture of the Central University, to Shandong to inspect. They have now returned to Beijing and decided to build it at Riguan Peak. It is currently being designed and will begin construction in February. It will cost about 20,000 yuan. The instruments and radios have already been prepared. In addition, the institute sent Hu Zhenduo to Gansu to set up an observatory in Suzhou. Hu has arrived in Lanzhou and will go to Suzhou in a few days to prepare for the construction. (Central News Agency, 8th)

The Ministry of Communications Improves Telephones in Nanchang 67

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications has decided to build a complete telephone system in Nanchang. It is currently selecting a bureau site, purchasing and allocating equipment, and assigning technicians to be responsible for the construction, which is limited to eight months. (Central News Agency, 8th)

The Measurement of the Bengbu-Zheng Branch Line of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Begins 68

(Nanjing) The Tianjin-Pukou Railway Bengbu-Zheng Branch Line has appointed more than ten engineers, including Yang Liren, to depart from Bengbu and begin surveying. It is scheduled to be completed in one month and completed in three months. (Central News Agency, 8th)

Cremation of Luosang Nangjia's Remains 69

(Nanjing) On the morning of the 8th, Luosang Nangjia's remains were wrapped in sandalwood, sulfur, and thick cloth according to Tibetan customs and sent into the seated vat. At about 8:00, they were cremated at Qingliang Mountain. Hundreds of monks, lamas, staff members of the Mongolian and Tibetan Association and the Panchen Lama's office, and others attended the funeral. More than 2,000 people observed the funeral. It took two days and nights for the remains to turn into ashes. The ashes will be transported to Mongolia for burial. (Central News Agency, 8th)

The Central Government Appoints Anhui Provincial Party Affairs Design Committee 70

(Nanjing) After the Central Government appointed Miao Peicheng as the Anhui Provincial Party Affairs Commissioner and other members, it also appointed seven people, including Hu Yiguan, as design committee members. The 111th Central Standing Committee has now appointed Wu Zunming as the secretary-general of the provincial party headquarters. (Central News Agency, 8th)

Agricultural Experimental Station Sends Personnel to Japan for Inspection 71

(Nanjing) The Central Agricultural Experimental Station plans to open various farms and has purchased land in Cunlingwei to conduct various agricultural experiments. Because agriculture in Japan is developed, it has sent technician Lin Gang to Japan to inspect the agricultural experimental fields in various parts of the country in order to learn from them. (Special dispatch, 8th)

The Ministry of Communications Recruits Postal Trainees 72

(Nanjing) In order to cultivate postal savings and remittance personnel, the Ministry of Communications is recruiting six trainees to be sent to Guangdong to study postal savings and remittance services, as the postal savings system in Guangdong is the most complete. The recruitment outline has 11 articles, and registration began at the ministry on the 7th and the examination will be held on April 1. (Special dispatch, 8th)

The Nanjing Social Affairs Bureau Plans to Correct the Decoration of Storefronts 73

(Nanjing) The Social Affairs Bureau has found that there are many reasons for the closure of stores in Nanjing, mainly due to the recession. However, most stores only pay attention to the decoration of storefronts and do not focus on practical matters. Once business is sluggish, they cannot sustain themselves. In the future, we should find ways to correct this. (Special dispatch, 8th)

The Jiangxi Provincial Government Requests a Subsidy for Political Expenses 74

(Nanjing) Xiong Shihui, the chairman of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, has submitted a request for a monthly subsidy of 250,000 yuan for political expenses, citing the precedents of other provinces, due to the province's financial difficulties. After receiving the submission, the government stated that the province's collection of excessive surcharges on land taxes and department store taxes was trivial and that the subsidies could only be approved after the above-mentioned taxes were abolished. (Special dispatch, 8th)

Shi Qingyang Requests a Month's Leave 75

(Nanjing) Shi Qingyang, Chairman of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, has requested a month's leave from the Executive Yuan for recuperation due to physical weakness. During his leave, the affairs of the committee will be handled by Vice Chairman Zhao Pilian. (Special dispatch, 8th)

The Italian Embassy Representative in Beijing is Recalled 76

(Nanjing) Fei Xiaoyue Luo, the representative of the Italian Embassy in China in Beijing, was the former Minister to China. He has now been recalled to his country by the Italian government. Fei is scheduled to go to Shanghai on the night of the 8th and wait for the Empress of Canada to return home on the 12th. He will stay in Italy for about four months and then return to China to resume his duties. He went to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to bid farewell to our diplomatic representatives. All duties in Beijing will be temporarily handled by the embassy secretary, Anfuso. Mr. An arrived in Beijing on the morning of the 8th and went to the office of the Italian Minister in Beijing, located on Tieguan Lane, to take office. (Special dispatch, 8th)

The Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission Pays Attention to the Massacre of Overseas Chinese in Siam 77

(Nanjing) Regarding the massacre of overseas Chinese by Siamese police, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission has recently telegraphed Jiang Zuobin, the minister to Japan, requesting him to negotiate with the Siamese ambassador to Japan in order to achieve the goal of punishing the murderers and compensating for the losses. (Special dispatch, 8th)

Beijing Women's Circles Commemorate March 8th 78

(Nanjing) The Beijing women's circles held a national women's festival at Nanjing Girls' High School at noon on the 8th, with more than 1,000 people attending. It was resolved to send a telegram to women across the country to unanimously use domestic products, promote new life, and ask the government to strictly enforce the prohibition of prostitution, establish large-scale women's factories, accommodate female employees as much as possible in various agencies, set up childcare centers, and ban newspapers that insult women. After the meeting, entertainment performances were also given. (Central News Agency, 8th)

The Yangtze River Water Conservancy Association Will Hold a Plenary Meeting Today 79

(Nanjing) The Yangtze River Water Conservancy Association will hold a plenary committee meeting on the 9th. The attendees will include Zheng Hangyu and Chen Zhanen from the Ministry of Interior, Li Dihou from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, An Jingfu from the Ministry of Finance, Liu Yinfei from the Ministry of Industry, Chen Maoxie from the Construction Committee, Xia Guangyu from the Ministry of Railways, Xia Tingzi from the Ministry of Communications, and Xi Dejiong, Ma Yiqun, and Blanc Duhamel, and more than ten other people. The meeting will discuss various issues related to the association's affairs in the future. Song Xishang, the director of the engineering office, will also rush back from Changyuan to participate. It is planned that plenary meetings will be held every two months thereafter. Zhao Zhiyou's inspection of the Yangtze River must wait until the meeting is completed before it can take place. (Special dispatch, 8th)

The Capital Afforestation Association Holds a Meeting 80

(Nanjing) The Capital Afforestation Association held its second meeting on the 8th. It was resolved that the tree planting ceremony to commemorate the death of the Prime Minister would be held at 1:00 PM on the 12th. Chen Gongbo was appointed as the chairman of the conference. The Air Force was requested to send aircraft to distribute slogans, and famous people were urged to broadcast speeches on the central radio station. (Special dispatch, 8th)

Huang Shaoxiong Will Inspect Various Provinces 81

(Nanjing) Huang Shaoxiong plans to go to various provinces to inspect civil administration and has submitted a request to the Executive Yuan for instructions. He will leave as soon as it is approved. (Special dispatch, 8th)
